\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
Gauss-\/\+Kronrod-\/\+Patterson quadrature coefficients for use in QUADPACK routine QNG. These coefficients were calculated with 101 decimal digit arithmetic by L. W. Fullerton, Bell Labs, Nov 1981.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Tp , typename Func\+Tp $>$ \\
auto emsr\+::cquad\+\_\+integrate (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{structemsr_1_1cquad__workspace}{cquad\+\_\+workspace}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, std\+::invoke\+\_\+result\+\_\+t$<$ Func\+Tp, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}} $>$$>$ \&}]{ws,  }\item[{Func\+Tp}]{func,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{a,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{b,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{epsabs,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{epsrel }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) -\/$>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structemsr_1_1adaptive__integral__t}{adaptive\+\_\+integral\+\_\+t}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, std\+::invoke\+\_\+result\+\_\+t$<$Func\+Tp, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}$>$$>$     }

CQUAD is a new doubly-\/adaptive general-\/purpose quadrature routine which can handle most types of singularities, non-\/numerical function values such as Inf or NaN, as well as some divergent integrals. It generally requires more function evaluations than the other integration routines in this library, yet fails less often for difficult integrands.

The underlying algorithm uses a doubly-\/adaptive scheme in which Clenshaw-\/\+Curtis quadrature rules of increasing degree are used to compute the integral in each interval. The L\+\_\+2-\/norm of the difference between the underlying interpolatory polynomials of two successive rules is used as an error estimate. The interval is subdivided if the difference between two successive rules is too large or a rule of maximum degree has been reached.

The CQUAD algorithm divides the integration region into subintervals, and in each iteration, the subinterval with the largest estimated error is processed. The algorithm uses Clenshaw-\/\+Curtis quadrature rules of degree 4, 8, 16 and 32 over 5, 9, 17 and 33 nodes respectively. Each interval is initialized with the lowest-\/degree rule. When an interval is processed, the next-\/higher degree rule is evaluated and an error estimate is computed based on the L\+\_\+2-\/norm of the difference between the underlying interpolating polynomials of both rules. If the highest-\/degree rule has already been used, or the interpolatory polynomials differ significantly, the interval is bisected. 

Definition at line 149 of file cquad\+\_\+integrate.\+tcc.

Integrate a smooth function from a to b.

Higher-\/order rules converge more rapidly for most functions, but may slow convergence for less well-\/behaved ones.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em func} & The function to be integrated. \\
\hline
{\em lower} & The lower limit of integration. \\
\hline
{\em upper} & The upper limit of integration. \\
\hline

\hline
{\em max\+\_\+rel\+\_\+error} & The relative error limit. \\
\hline
{\em max\+\_\+iter} & is the maximum number of iterations allowed \\
\hline
{\em qkintrule} & is the Gauss-\/\+Kronrod integration rule. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A structure containing the integration result and the error.

\[ \int_{0}^{+\infty}f(x)dx \] Making the change of variables\+: \[ x = exp\left[\frac{\pi}{2}sinh(u)\right], dx = \frac{\pi}{2} cosh(u) exp\left[\frac{\pi}{2}sinh(u)\right]du \] gives the following integral\+: \[ \int_{0}^{+\infty}f(exp\left[\frac{\pi}{2}sinh(u)\right]) = \sum_{k=-n}^{+n} \]

This function allows a non-\/zero lower limit {\ttfamily a}.

\end{DoxyParams}

\index{emsr@{emsr}!integrate\_singular\_endpoints@{integrate\_singular\_endpoints}}
\index{integrate\_singular\_endpoints@{integrate\_singular\_endpoints}!emsr@{emsr}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{integrate\_singular\_endpoints()}{integrate\_singular\_endpoints()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Tp , typename Func\+Tp $>$ \\
auto emsr\+::integrate\+\_\+singular\+\_\+endpoints (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Func\+Tp}]{func,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{lower,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{upper,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{alpha,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{beta,  }\item[{int}]{mu,  }\item[{int}]{nu,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{max\+\_\+abs\+\_\+error,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{max\+\_\+rel\+\_\+error,  }\item[{std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{max\+\_\+iter = {\ttfamily 1024} }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) -\/$>$  \mbox{\hyperlink{structemsr_1_1adaptive__integral__t}{adaptive\+\_\+integral\+\_\+t}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, std\+::invoke\+\_\+result\+\_\+t$<$ Func\+Tp, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}} $>$$>$}

The singular weight function is defined by\+: \[ W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta log^\mu (x-a) log^\nu (b-x) \] where $ \alpha > -1 $, $ \beta > -1 $, and $ \mu = 0 $, 1, $ \nu = 0, 1 $.

The weight function can take four different forms depending on the values of \textbackslash{}mu and \textbackslash{}nu, \[ W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta (\mu = 0, \nu = 0) W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta log(x-a) (\mu = 1, \nu = 0) W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta log(b-x) (\mu = 0, \nu = 1) W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta log(x-a) log(b-x) (\mu = 1, \nu = 1) \]

The QAWS algorithm is designed for integrands with algebraic-\/logarithmic singularities at the end-\/points of an integration region. \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespaceemsr_ae06aea07d280214f87920f34f9803426}\label{namespaceemsr_ae06aea07d280214f87920f34f9803426}} 
\index{emsr@{emsr}!integrate\_singular\_lower\_minf@{integrate\_singular\_lower\_minf}}
\index{integrate\_singular\_lower\_minf@{integrate\_singular\_lower\_minf}!emsr@{emsr}}

\[ \int_{-\infty}^{+\infty}f(x)dx \] Making the change of variables\+: \[ x = sinh\left[\frac{\pi}{2}sinh(u)\right], dx = \frac{\pi}{2} cosh(u) cosh\left[\frac{\pi}{2}sinh(u)\right]du \] gives the following integral\+: \[ \int_{-\infty}^{+\infty}f(sinh\left[\frac{\pi}{2}sinh(u)\right]) = \sum_{k=-n}^{+n} \]

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Tp , typename Func\+Tp , typename Integrator  = gauss\+\_\+kronrod\+\_\+integral$<$\+Tp$>$$>$ \\
auto emsr\+::qag\+\_\+integrate (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classemsr_1_1integration__workspace}{integration\+\_\+workspace}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, std\+::invoke\+\_\+result\+\_\+t$<$ Func\+Tp, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}} $>$$>$ \&}]{workspace,  }\item[{Func\+Tp}]{func,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{lower,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{upper,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{max\+\_\+abs\+\_\+err,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{max\+\_\+rel\+\_\+err,  }\item[{Integrator}]{quad = {\ttfamily gauss\+\_\+kronrod\+\_\+integral$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}$>$(Kronrod\+\_\+21)} }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) -\/$>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structemsr_1_1adaptive__integral__t}{adaptive\+\_\+integral\+\_\+t}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, std\+::invoke\+\_\+result\+\_\+t$<$Func\+Tp, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}$>$$>$     }

Integrates a function from finite a to finite b using an adaptive quadrature rule. The integration domain is recursively subdivided prioritized by the segment with the greatest absolute error estimate. Subdivision continues until a prescribed error target is reached or until a maximum number of divisions is performed.

Once either the absolute or relative error limit is reached, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceemsr_ab1b018f7a2028aa2b214e43ea271abee}{qag\+\_\+integrate()}} returns


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Func\+Tp} & A function type that takes a single real scalar argument and returns a real scalar. \\
\hline
{\em Tp} & A real type for the limits of integration and the step. \\
\hline
{\em Integrator} & A non-\/adaptive integrator that is able to return an error estimate in addition to the result.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em workspace} & The workspace that manages adaptive quadrature \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em func} & The single-\/variable function to be integrated \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em lower} & The lower limit of integration \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em upper} & The upper limit of integration \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em max\+\_\+abs\+\_\+err} & The limit on absolute error \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em max\+\_\+rel\+\_\+err} & The limit on relative error \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em quad} & The quadrature stepper taking a function object and two integration limits\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A tuple with the first value being the integration result, and the second value being the estimated error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

Adaptively integrate a function with known singular/discontinuous points.

{\em Func\+Tp} & A function type that takes a single real scalar argument and returns a real scalar. \\

{\em Tp} & A real type for the limits of integration and the step. \\
\hline
{\em Integrator} & A non-\/adaptive integrator that is able to return an error estimate in addition to the result.\\

Adaptively integrate a potentially singular function from a to b using a recursive Gauss-\/\+Kronrod algorithm.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Func\+Tp} & A function type that takes a single real scalar argument and returns a real scalar. \\
\hline
{\em Tp} & A real type for the limits of integration and the step. \\
\hline
{\em Integrator} & A non-\/adaptive integrator that is able to return an error estimate in addition to the result.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em workspace} & The workspace that manages adaptive quadrature \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em func} & The single-\/variable function to be integrated \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em pts} & The sorted array of points including the integration limits and intermediate discontinuities/singularities \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em max\+\_\+abs\+\_\+err} & The limit on absolute error \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em max\+\_\+rel\+\_\+err} & The limit on relative error \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em quad} & The quadrature stepper taking a function object and two integration limits \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Tp , typename Func\+Tp , typename Integrator  = gauss\+\_\+kronrod\+\_\+integral$<$\+Tp$>$$>$ \\
auto emsr\+::qawc\+\_\+integrate (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classemsr_1_1integration__workspace}{integration\+\_\+workspace}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, std\+::invoke\+\_\+result\+\_\+t$<$ Func\+Tp, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}} $>$$>$ \&}]{workspace,  }\item[{Func\+Tp}]{func,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{lower,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{upper,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{center,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{max\+\_\+abs\+\_\+err,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{max\+\_\+rel\+\_\+err,  }\item[{Integrator}]{quad = {\ttfamily gauss\+\_\+kronrod\+\_\+integral$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}$>$(Kronrod\+\_\+15)} }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) -\/$>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structemsr_1_1adaptive__integral__t}{adaptive\+\_\+integral\+\_\+t}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, std\+::invoke\+\_\+result\+\_\+t$<$Func\+Tp, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}$>$$>$     }

Adaptive integration for Cauchy principal values\+: \[ I = \int_a^b dx f(x) / (x - c) \] The adaptive bisection algorithm of QAG is used, with modifications to ensure that subdivisions do not occur at the singular point x = c. When a subinterval contains the point x = c or is close to it then a special 25-\/point modified Clenshaw-\/\+Curtis rule is used to control the singularity. Further away from the singularity the algorithm uses a user-\/supplied integration rule (default 15-\/point Gauss-\/\+Kronrod). 

Definition at line 61 of file qawc\+\_\+integrate.\+tcc.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{qaws\_integrate()}{qaws\_integrate()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Tp , typename Func\+Tp , typename Integrator  = gauss\+\_\+kronrod\+\_\+integral$<$\+Tp$>$$>$ \\
auto emsr\+::qaws\+\_\+integrate (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classemsr_1_1integration__workspace}{integration\+\_\+workspace}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, std\+::invoke\+\_\+result\+\_\+t$<$ Func\+Tp, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}} $>$$>$ \&}]{workspace,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{structemsr_1_1qaws__integration__table}{qaws\+\_\+integration\+\_\+table}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}} $>$ \&}]{table,  }\item[{Func\+Tp}]{func,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{lower,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{upper,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{max\+\_\+abs\+\_\+err,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{max\+\_\+rel\+\_\+err,  }\item[{Integrator}]{quad = {\ttfamily gauss\+\_\+kronrod\+\_\+integral$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}$>$(Kronrod\+\_\+15)} }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) -\/$>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structemsr_1_1adaptive__integral__t}{adaptive\+\_\+integral\+\_\+t}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, std\+::invoke\+\_\+result\+\_\+t$<$Func\+Tp, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}$>$$>$     }

The singular weight function is defined by\+: \[ W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta log^\mu (x-a) log^\nu (b-x) \] where $ \alpha > -1 $, $ \beta > -1 $, and $ \mu = 0 $, 1, $ \nu = 0, 1 $.

The weight function can take four different forms depending on the values of \textbackslash{}mu and \textbackslash{}nu, \[ W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta (\mu = 0, \nu = 0) W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta log(x-a) (\mu = 1, \nu = 0) W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta log(b-x) (\mu = 0, \nu = 1) W(x) = (x-a)^\alpha (b-x)^\beta log(x-a) log(b-x) (\mu = 1, \nu = 1) \]

The QAWS algorithm is designed for integrands with algebraic-\/logarithmic singularities at the end-\/points of an integration region.

In order to work efficiently the algorithm requires a precomputed table of Chebyshev moments. 

Definition at line 88 of file qaws\+\_\+integrate.\+tcc.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{qc25c()}{qc25c()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Tp , typename Func\+Tp , typename Integrator  = gauss\+\_\+kronrod\+\_\+integral$<$\+Tp$>$$>$ \\
auto emsr\+::qc25c (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Func\+Tp}]{func,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{lower,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{upper,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}}]{center,  }\item[{Integrator}]{quad }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) -\/$>$  std\+::tuple$<$ decltype(\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}\{\} $\ast$func(\mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}\{\})), \mbox{\hyperlink{test__integral_8tcc_a82f489a4943d33943d0b0f781a801283}{Tp}}, bool $>$}

Adaptive integration for Cauchy principal values\+: \[ I = \int_a^b dx f(x) / (x - c) \] The adaptive bisection algorithm of QAG is used, with modifications to ensure that subdivisions do not occur at the singular point x = c. When a subinterval contains the point x = c or is close to it then a special 25-\/point modified Clenshaw-\/\+Curtis rule is used to control the singularity. Further away from the singularity the algorithm uses a user-\/supplied integration rule. 

Definition at line 214 of file qawc\+\_\+integrate.\+tcc.

\index{emsr@{emsr}!s\_tridiag\_symm@{s\_tridiag\_symm}}
\index{s\_tridiag\_symm@{s\_tridiag\_symm}!emsr@{emsr}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{s\_tridiag\_symm()}{s\_tridiag\_symm()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Rand\+Acc\+Iter , typename Rand\+Acc\+Iter\+RHS $>$ \\
int emsr\+::s\+\_\+tridiag\+\_\+symm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{n,  }\item[{Rand\+Acc\+Iter \&}]{diag,  }\item[{Rand\+Acc\+Iter \&}]{subd,  }\item[{Rand\+Acc\+Iter\+RHS \&}]{rhs }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Diagonalize a symmetric tridiagonal matrix. 

This routine is a slightly modified version of the EISPACK routine to perform the implicit QL algorithm on a symmetric tridiagonal matrix.

It has been modified to produce the product Q\textquotesingle{} $\ast$ Z, where Z is an input vector and Q is the orthogonal matrix diagonalizing the input matrix. ~\newline
 The changes consist (essentialy) of applying the orthogonal transformations directly to Z as they are generated.

Original C++ version by John Burkardt (GPL).

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Sylvan Elhay, Jaroslav Kautsky, Algorithm 655\+: IQPACK, FORTRAN Subroutines for the Weights of Interpolatory Quadrature, ACM Transactions on Mathematical Software, Volume 13, Number 4, December 1987, pages 399-\/415.

Roger Martin, James Wilkinson, The Implicit QL Algorithm, Numerische Mathematik, Volume 12, Number 5, December 1968, pages 377-\/383.
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em n} & The order of the matrix. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em diag} & The diagonal entries \mbox{[}0, n-\/1\mbox{]} of the matrix. On output, the information in diag is overwritten. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em subd} & The subdiagonal entries of the matrix, in entries \mbox{[}0, n-\/2\mbox{]}. On output, the information in subd is overwritten. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em rhs} & On input, a vector. On output, the value of Q\textquotesingle{} $\ast$ Z, where Q is the matrix that diagonalizes the input symmetric tridiagonal matrix. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
